Crescent Sighting: Large Multitude in Clear Skies
Expands on the requirement of a large multitude for crescent sighting in clear skies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a large multitude is required for crescent testimony in clear sky conditions according to the Hanafi school, and identify the mufta bihi position that the imam determines the number based on widespread reporting.

Core Idea
When the sky is clear, a large multitude is required; the imam decides the number based on tawatur, not a fixed count.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah examines the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of witnesses required for crescent sighting when the sky is clear. While the Zahir al-Riwaya insists on a large multitude, other Hanafi authorities accept fewer witnesses under special conditions. The text traces the different opinions and concludes with the relied-upon position that the imam exercises discretion based on tawatur (widespread reporting). Understanding this dispute is essential for applying the ruling in diverse settings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its rationale
When there is no obstruction in the sky (clear), the text states a large multitude is necessary. The rationale: the sighting place is unified, eyesight is sound, and intentions are sincere, so a lone claim raises suspicion of error. Therefore, the community must wait until many people see it.
The ruling applies to both Ramadan and Eid al-Fitr.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi divergence from Zahir al-Riwaya
The text reports that Imam Abu Hanifa was satisfied with two witnesses (as in other testimonies), and al-Tahawi accepted a single just witness from outside the city. Zahir al-Din accepted one witness on a high place. These views are contrary to the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwaya) that demands a large multitude.
Al-Tahawi's view is based on istihsan (juristic preference) due to fewer obstacles outside the city.
3
Understand the later development and acceptance of exceptions
Later authorities like al-Marghinani and the author of al-Fatawa al-Sughra relied on al-Tahawi's view, especially considering people's laziness in religious matters. The passage lists various opinions on the number of the 'large multitude': the whole neighborhood, 50 (by Abu Yusuf, analogy to qasama), 500, etc., showing no fixed number.
Al-Kamal notes that the correct view is from Muhammad and Abu Yusuf: the criterion is tawatur (widespread reporting from all sides).
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The text concludes that the matter is delegated to the imam's opinion, as the number varies with time and place. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa, combining flexibility and practicality while preserving the requirement of widespread certainty.
Thus, the requirement of a 'large multitude' is not a fixed number but a contextual standard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا لم يكن بالسماء علة فلا بد من جمع عظيم لرمضان والفطر وغيرهما لأن المطلع متحد في ذلك المحل والموانع منتفية والأبصار سليمة والهمم في طلب رؤية الهلال مستقيمة فالتفرد في مثل هذه الحالة لوهم الغلط فوجب التوقف في رؤية البعض القليل حتى يراه الجمع الكثير وروي عن الإمام أنه يكتفي بشهادة اثنين كسائر الحقوق ولا فرق في ظاهر الرواية بين أهل المصر وبين من ورد من خارج المصر وذكر الطحاوي أنه يقبل شهادة الواحد العدل إذا جاء من خارج المصر لقلة الموانع وإليه الإشارة في كتاب الاستحسان وهما خلاف ظاهر الرواية وكذا لا فرق بين ما لو كان على مكان مرتفع في المصر أو غيره خلافا لما اختاره الإمام ظهير الدين من قبوله إذا كان بمرتفع وكذا اعتمد قول الطحاوي الإمام المرغيناني وصاحب الأقضية والفتاوى الصغرى كذا في الدراية وفي التجنيس لو كانت السماء مصحية تقبل شهادة الواحد إذا رأى هلال رمضان خارج المصر وكذا إذا رآه في المصر على مكان مرتفع لأنه انفرد عن غيره بالموجب للرؤية فعدم رؤية غيره لا يقدح في شهادته انتهى لأن الهواء في الصحراء أصفى ويتفق لمن كان على مكان مرتفع ما لا يتفق لمن دونه في الموقف كذا في الدراية وقال الشيخ زين والعلامة المقدسي في شرحيهما ينبغي أن يعمل بهذا في هذا الزمان لتكاسل الناس في الأمور الدينية ومقدار الجمع العظيم قيل أهل المحلة وعن أبي يوسف خمسون كالقسامة وعن خلف خمس مائة ببلخ قليل وقال بعضهم من كل جماعة واحد أو اثنان وقال البقالي الألف ببخارى قليل وقال الكمال الحق ما روي عن محمد وأبي يوسف أيضا أن العبرة بتواتر الخبر ومجيئه من كل جانب انتهى وفي التجنيس وعن محمد أنه يفوض أمر القلة والكثرة إلى ما رأى الإمام وهو الصحيح لأن ذلك يختلف باختلاف الأوقات والأماكن فكان
And if there is no cause in the sky, then a large multitude is necessary for Ramaḍān and Fitr and others, because the sighting place is unified in that location, the obstacles are absent, the eyesight is sound, and the intentions in seeking the sighting of the crescent are straight. So being alone in such a situation leads to suspicion of error, so it became necessary to withhold regarding the sighting of a small few until a large multitude sees it. And it is narrated from the Imam that he is satisfied with the testimony of two, like other rights. And there is no difference in Ẓāhir al-Riwāya between the people of the city and those who come from outside the city. Al-Ṭaḥāwī mentioned that the testimony of a single just person is accepted if he comes from outside the city due to the scarcity of obstacles, and reference is made to this in Kitāb al-Istiḥsān, and these two are contrary to Ẓāhir al-Riwāya. Likewise, there is no difference between whether he was on a high place in the city or elsewhere, contrary to what Imām Ẓahīr al-Dīn chose of acceptance if he is on a high place. Likewise, Imām al-Marghīnānī and the author of al-Aqḍiya and al-Fatāwā al-Ṣughrā relied on the statement of al-Ṭaḥāwī. So it is in al-Dirāya. In al-Tajnīs: If the sky is clear, the testimony of one is accepted if he sees the crescent of Ramaḍān outside the city, and likewise if he sees it in the city on a high place, because he is unique in having the cause for sighting, so the failure of others to see it does not detract from his testimony. This is because the air in the desert is clearer, and what occurs to one on a high place does not occur to those below in the standpoint. So it is in al-Dirāya. And Shaykh Zayn and al-ʿAllāma al-Maqdisī said in their commentaries: It is appropriate to act upon this in this era due to people's laziness in religious matters. And the number of the large multitude: It was said: the inhabitants of the neighborhood; from Abū Yūsuf: fifty, like qasāma; from Khalaf: five hundred is little in Balkh; some said: from each group one or two; al-Baqqālī said: a thousand is little in Bukhārā; and al-Kamāl said: The truth is what is narrated from Muḥammad and Abū Yūsuf that the criterion is the tawātur of the report and its coming from every side. In al-Tajnīs: from Muḥammad that he delegates the matter of fewness and manyness to the opinion of the imam, and this is the correct view, because that differs according to times and places.
Source pages p. 635

Commentary
This section addresses the situation when the sky is clear (no cloud cover). The commentator notes that a large multitude (al-jamʿ al-ʿaẓīm) is required for both Ramaḍān and Eid al-Fitr because when conditions are optimal, the moon should be widely visible. A small number claiming sighting raises suspicion of error. Interestingly, there is a narration that Imam Abū Ḥanīfa himself was satisfied with two witnesses, as in other legal matters, but the Ẓāhir al-Riwāya insists on a large multitude. Several positions are then presented: al-Ṭaḥāwī accepts a single just witness if he comes from outside the city (due to fewer obstacles), and Imām Ẓahīr al-Dīn accepts one on a high place. The commentator notes that these are contrary to the Ẓāhir al-Riwāya, but later authorities like al-Marghīnānī and the author of al-Fatāwā al-Ṣughrā rely on al-Ṭaḥāwī's view. The commentary concludes with the definition of the large multitude, offering various opinions: the entire neighborhood (ahl al-mahalla), fifty (by Abū Yūsuf, analogizing to oaths in qasāma), five hundred (in Balkh), one or two from each group, a thousand (in Bukhārā). The most correct view, according to al-Kamāl and Muḥammad, is that the criterion is tawātur (widespread reporting) and that the imam should decide based on time and place. This shows the Ḥanafī school's flexibility in adapting legal rulings to context.

Key Terms
الجمع العظيم (al-jamʿ al-ʿaẓīm): A large multitude of witnesses whose number is not fixed but depends on context; it contrasts with the requirement of two witnesses in ordinary cases.
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāya): The well-known transmitted rulings from the founding imams, as opposed to exceptional or weaker narrations.
تواتر (tawātur): Widespread reporting from multiple sides that removes doubt; used here as the criterion for the large multitude.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Ḥanafī position in this text, what is the proper way to determine the required number of witnesses for the crescent when the sky is clear?
A) Always two witnesses, as in other legal matters
B) Fifty witnesses, by analogy to qasāma
C) The imam decides based on widespread reporting (tawātur) and local circumstances
D) A single witness from outside the city is always sufficient

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's mufta bihi on crescent sighting in clear skies is that the number of witnesses is left to the imam's judgment based on widespread reporting, allowing flexibility across times and places.

Crescent Testimony: Sky Condition, Witness Count, and Completing Thirty Days
Rulings on crescent sighting testimony with clear and cloudy skies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on completing thirty days of Ramadan when the Shawwal crescent is not seen, differentiating based on sky condition and number of witnesses, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of crescent testimony depends on whether the sky is clear or cloudy, and on the number of witnesses.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah addresses a practical scenario: when thirty days of Ramadan are completed but the Shawwal crescent is not sighted. The ruling depends on two factors: the presence of clouds and how many witnesses established Ramadan. These factors determine whether the community should break fast or fast an additional day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two variables
Note that the ruling hinges on (1) sky condition: clear (mus.hiyah) or cloudy (mutaghayyimah), and (2) the number of witnesses whose testimony established Ramadan: a single witness or two witnesses.
The term 'cloudy' includes any obstruction like fog, dust, etc.
2
Apply the rule for a single witness with clear sky
If Ramadan was established by a single witness and the sky is clear, there is consensus that the community does NOT break fast after 30 days; they must fast an additional day.
The clear sky indicates the witness was likely mistaken.
3
Apply the rule for two witnesses with clear sky
If two witnesses established Ramadan and the sky is clear, there is a dispute: some Hanafi authorities say they break fast (like eyewitness), but the preferred view (mufta bihi) is they do NOT break fast due to apparent error.
This is the main point of ikhtilaf covered in the passage.
4
Apply the rule for cloudy sky (consensus)
If the sky is cloudy, regardless of whether Ramadan was established by one or two witnesses, the community breaks fast after 30 days – by consensus.
Clouds provide an excuse for not sighting, so testimony stands.
5
Note the role of the Imam's discretion
The exact number for a 'large multitude' (al-jam' al-'azim) when required is not fixed; it is delegated to the Imam's judgment, varying by time and place.
This applies when the sky is clear and multiple witnesses are needed for initial testimony.

وإذا لم يكن بالسَّماءِ عِلَّةٌ، فلا بد من جَمْعِ عظيم لرمضانَ والفِطْرِ. ومقدارُ الجَمْعِ العَظِيمِ قيل: أهل المحلة، وعن أبي يوسف: خمسون كالقسامة، وعن خلف: خمس مائة ببلخ قليل وقال بعضهم: من كل جماعة واحد أو اثنان، وقال « البقالي : الألف «ببخارى» قليل، وقال « الكمال » : الحق ما روي عن «محمد» و «أبي يوسف» أيضاً أن العبرة بتواتر الخبر ومجيئه من كل جانب، انتهى. وفي ( التجنيس » : وعن ( محمد » : أنه يفوض أمر القلـة والكثرة إلى ما رأى الإمام وهو الصحيح؛ لأن ذلك يختلف باختلاف الأوقات والأماكن فكان مفوض إلى رأي الإمام في الأصح. وإذا تم العدد بشهادة فرد، ولم يُرَ هلالُ الفِطر، والسَّماءُ مُصْحِيَةٌ، لا يَحِلُّ لَهُ الفِطْرُ. وَاخْتُلِفَ الترجيح فيما إذا كان بشهادةِ عَدْلَيْنِ، ولا خلاف في حِلَّ الفِطْرِ إذا كان بالسَّماءِ علة، ولو ثَبَتَ رمضان بشهادة الفرد. المحكم فيه رأي الإمام، انتهى. وكذا في «البرهان»، فهو (مُفَوَّض إلى رأي الإمام، في الأصح) لتفاوت الناس صدقاً. (وإذا تم العدد) أي: عدد رمضان ثلاثين ( بشهادة) واحـــد (فرد) أي: منفرد برؤيته ( ولم يَرَ هلالَ الفِطْرِ ، و ذلك و ( السَّماءُ مُصْحِيَةٌ ، لا يَحِلُّ لَهُ الفِطْرُ) اتفاقاً علـى مـا ذکره شمس الأئمة الحلواني» كما سنذكره. وقال في الدرر والغرر ويعزر ذلك الشاهد انتهى. وفي «التجنيس » : إذا لم ير هلال شوال لا يفطرون حتى يصوموا يوماً آخر، لأنَّ الرمضانيــة فـي حــق ثبوت الفطر عند إكمال العدة لم تثبت بهذه الشهادة انتهى ذكر حكم مذهبنا غير مسند لقـائل مـن غير تفصيل، وقال الزيلعي والأشبه أن يقال: إن كانت السماء مصحية لا يفطرون لظهور غلطه، وإن كانت مغيمة يفطرون لعدم ظهور الغلط انتهى. (واختُلِفَ الترجيحُ) في حل الفطر (فيما إذا كــان) ثبوت رمضان ( بشهادةِ عَدْلَيْنِ)، وتم العدد ولم يُر هلال شوال مع الصحو، صحيح في ( الدراية ) و « الخلاصة » و « البزازية) حل الفطر، و، ووجهه أن شهادة الشاهدين إذا قبلت كانت بمنزلة العيان، ولو عاينوا هلال رمضان يفطرون بعد إكمال ثلاثين، وإن لم يروا الهلال فكذلك هـا هنا، وفي « المجموع»، و« النوازل» : لا يفطرون وصححه، وكذلك السيد الإمام الأجل «ناصر الدين»، ووجهه أنَّ السماء لو كانت مصحية وثبت هلال رمضان كان عدم رؤية غيرهما دليلاً على غلطهما، حتى لا تقبل شهادتهما، فكذلك عدم الرؤية بعد إكمال ثلاثين يوماً من وقت رؤيتهما، وإذا كانت السماء مصحيَّة دليل على الغلط، فتبطل بذلك شهادتهما، كذا في «التجنيس » ، وقال « الكمال»: لا يبعد لـو قال قائل: إن قبلهما في الصحو :أي: لأمر قام عنده، وتم العدد لا يفطرون، وإن قبلهما في غيم أفطروا لتحقق زيادة القوة في الثبوت في الثاني، والاشتراك في عدم الثبوت أصلاً في الأول، فصار كشهادة الواحد، ولا خلاف في حِلِّ الفِطْرِ إذا تم العدد و (كَانَ بالسَّماءِ عِلَّةٌ ، ولو) وصلية، (ثَبَتَ رمضانُ بشهادة الفرد العدل كالعدلين، كما ذكره شمس الأئمة قال في ( التجنيس» : إذا شهد اثنان وتم والسماء متغيمة يفطرون بالاتفاق انتهى وقال في مجمع الروايات » : قال « الزاهدي»: لو قبل الإمام شهادة الواحد وأتموا ثلاثين ثم غم عليهم هلال شوال، قال أبو حنيفة وأبو يوسف رحمهما الله : يصومون من الغد وقال محمد: يفطرون، وقال شمس الأئمة ( الحلواني رحمه الله الخلاف فيما إذا لم ير هلال شوال والسماء مصحية، فإن كانت متغيرة يفطرون بلا خلاف انتهى وكذا في « الذخيرة»، وكذا في ( معراج الدراية» عن «المجتبى ) . وقوله في ( الهداية » : إذا قبل الإمام العدد
And if there is no cloud in the sky, then a large multitude is necessary for (testifying to) Ramadan and Fitr. And the measure of the large multitude: it is said: the people of the neighborhood; and from Abu Yusuf: fifty, like the oath of qasama; and from Khalaf: five hundred are few in Balkh; and some said: from each group one or two; and al-Baqqali said: a thousand are few in Bukhara; and al-Kamal said: the truth is what is narrated from Muhammad and Abu Yusuf as well that the criterion is the widespread news coming from every side, end. And in al-Tajnīs: from Muhammad: that he delegates the matter of few and many to what the Imam sees, and that is the correct view; because that differs with differences of times and places, so it is delegated to the opinion of the Imam in the most correct view. And when the number is completed by the testimony of an individual, and the crescent of Fitr is not seen, and the sky is clear, breaking fast is not permissible for him. And there is a difference in preference regarding when it is by the testimony of two just witnesses, and there is no difference in the permissibility of breaking fast if there is a cloud in the sky, even if Ramadan is established by the testimony of an individual. The decisive matter is the opinion of the Imam, end. Similarly in al-Burhan, so it is delegated to the opinion of the Imam in the most correct view, because people vary in truthfulness. (And when the number is completed) i.e., the number of Ramadan being thirty, by the testimony of an individual (fard), i.e., alone in his sighting, (and he did not see the crescent of Fitr, and the sky is clear, breaking fast is not permissible for him) unanimously, as mentioned by Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, as we will mention. And in al-Durr wa al-Ghurar: that witness is to be punished, end. And in al-Tajnīs: When the crescent of Shawwal is not seen, they do not break fast until they fast another day, because the Ramadan status with respect to the establishment of breaking fast upon completion of the number is not established by this testimony, end. He mentioned the ruling of our school, not attributed to any speaker, without detail. And al-Zayla'i said: The more appropriate is to say: if the sky is clear, they do not break fast due to the apparent error; and if it is cloudy, they break fast due to the absence of apparent error, end. (And there is a difference in preference) regarding the permissibility of breaking fast (when) Ramadan is established (by the testimony of two witnesses), and the number is completed and the crescent of Shawwal is not seen with clear sky. It is sahih in al-Diraya, al-Khulasa, and al-Bazzaziyya: breaking fast is permissible, and its justification is that when the testimony of two witnesses is accepted, it is like eyewitness; and if they had eyewitnessed the crescent of Ramadan, they would break fast after completing thirty days even if they do not see the crescent, so likewise here. And in al-Majmu' and al-Nawazil: they do not break fast, and he declared it sahih, and likewise the Sayyid al-Imam al-Ajal Nasir al-Din. Its justification is that if the sky were clear and the crescent of Ramadan were established, the failure of others to see it would be evidence of their error, even to the point that their testimony would not be accepted; so similarly, failure to see after completing thirty days from the time of their sighting (indicates error). And when the sky is clear, that is evidence of error, so their testimony is invalidated by that, as in al-Tajnīs. And al-Kamal said: It is not far-fetched if someone said: If he accepted their testimony in clear sky (i.e., due to a reason arising with him), and the number is completed, they do not break fast; but if he accepted their testimony in cloudy weather, they break fast, because the strength of establishment is increased in the second case, and there is no establishment at all in the first case, so it becomes like the testimony of a single witness. And there is no difference in the permissibility of breaking fast when the number is completed and (there is a cloud in the sky), even if Ramadan is established by the testimony of a single just witness, just like two witnesses, as mentioned by Shams al-A'imma. He said in al-Tajnīs: When two witnesses testify and (the number is completed) and the sky is cloudy, they break fast by consensus, end. And in Majma' al-Riwayat: al-Zahidi said: If the Imam accepts the testimony of one witness and they complete thirty days, then the crescent of Shawwal is concealed from them, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them) said: They fast the next day; and Muhammad said: They break fast. And Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: The difference is when the crescent of Shawwal is not seen and the sky is clear; if it is cloudy, they break fast without difference, end. Similarly in al-Dhakhira, and similarly in Mi'raj al-Diraya from al-Mujtaba. And his statement in al-Hidaya: When the Imam accepts the number.
Source pages p. 635

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah (a commentary on Nur al-Idah) discusses the legal rulings on the testimony for sighting the crescent moon for Ramadan and Eid al-Fitr. The author presents the Hanafi position with various opinions from the early jurists.

**Key points:**
1. **Sky condition and number of witnesses:** When the sky is clear (musihiyah), a large multitude (jam' 'azim) is required because the absence of clouds eliminates any excuse for not seeing the moon, so a single testimony is likely an error. When the sky is cloudy (mutaghayyimah), the testimony of two just witnesses suffices due to the inherent difficulty in sighting.
2. **Measure of 'large multitude':** There are multiple opinions: Abu Yusuf said fifty (analogy to qasama), Khalaf said five hundred, al-Baqqali said a thousand. The correct view attributed to Muhammad and Abu Yusuf is that the criterion is widespread news (tawatur) coming from every side. Ultimately, the matter is delegated to the Imam's discretion because conditions vary by time and place.
3. **Completion of 30 days without sighting Shawwal:** If Ramadan was established by a single witness and the sky is clear, one cannot break fast (by consensus). If established by two witnesses, there is a difference: some say they break fast (because the two witnesses are like eyewitnesses), others say they do not (because the clear sky indicates error). The preferred view (al-mu'tamad) is that if the sky is clear, they do not break fast; if cloudy, they do, by consensus.
4. **Intra-Hanafi difference:** Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that if Ramadan was established by a single witness and then 30 days are completed but the sky is clear, they must fast an additional day. Muhammad holds that they break fast. However, this difference applies only when the sky is clear; if cloudy, all agree they break fast.

The passage underscores the Hanafi reliance on practical considerations ('illa) and the Imam's discretion to resolve matters where texts are flexible.

Key Terms
الجمع العظيم (al-jam' al-'azim): A large group of people whose testimony is accepted without suspicion of error; its exact number is flexible and left to the Imam's discretion.
السَّماءُ مُصْحِيَةٌ (al-sama' mushiyah): Clear sky without clouds, where no obstacle prevents seeing the crescent.
العدد (al-'adad): The number of days completed, specifically 30 days of Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if Ramadan is established by the testimony of two just witnesses and 30 days are completed but the crescent of Shawwal is not seen, what is the ruling when the sky is clear?
A) They break fast by consensus.
B) They do not break fast because the clear sky indicates error.
C) They must fast one extra day, then break fast.
D) It depends on the Imam's decision.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on completing 30 days of Ramadan without sighting Shawwal hinges on the sky condition and the number of witnesses who established Ramadan, with the Imam's discretion playing a key role in determining the required multitude.

The Moon of Eid al-Adha: Like Shawwal, Not Ramadan
Ruling that the moon of Eid al-Adha is like Shawwal in testimony requirements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling for proving the moon of Dhul Hijjah and explain why it differs from the nawadir view of Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
The moon of Eid al-Adha requires the same testimony as Shawwal—two witnesses or a crowd—because of the widespread benefit of sacrifices.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: how many witnesses are needed to prove the start of Dhul Hijjah, the month of Hajj and Eid al-Adha. While a rare narration from Imam Abu Hanifa suggests one witness suffices, similar to Ramadan, the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwaya) equates it to Shawwal, requiring two witnesses or a large crowd. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly determining the date of Eid al-Adha and the timing of sacrifices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
Determine the ruling from the mainstream Hanafi sources (zahir al-riwaya) regarding the testimony needed for the moon of Dhul Hijjah.
This is the position that is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa).
2
Identify the opposing view within the school
Locate the alternate view attributed to Abu Hanifa from the nawadir (rare) transmissions. Note its content and source.
This view equates Dhul Hijjah with Ramadan.
3
Analyze the evidence for each view
Understand the rationale behind each view. For the relied-upon view, the benefit of sacrifices (manfa'at al-udhiya) necessitates stricter testimony to avoid confusion.
The opposing view may rely on analogy to Ramadan without considering the specific benefit.
4
Determine the relied-upon position (mufta bihi)
Confirm that the zahir al-riwaya position is the one adopted by the majority of later Hanafi scholars and is deemed 'al-ashah' (most correct).
The text explicitly states 'wa huwa al-ashah' and 'al-madhhab zahir al-riwaya'.
5
Apply the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Consider a real scenario: if one person claims to have seen the Dhul Hijjah moon, under the relied-upon position it is not accepted, but under the nawadir view it would be. This directly affects the date of Eid.
This step solidifies the importance of knowing the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وهلالُ الأضحى) في الحكم (كالة لر) فلابد من نصاب الشهادة مع العلة، والجمع العظيــم مــع الصحو، علـى ظاهر الرواية، وهو الأصح لما تعلق به من نفع العباد بلحوم الأضاحي، خلافاً لما يروى عن أبي حنيفة أنه كهلال رمضان، وهي رواية ( النوادر ) وصححها في «التحفة» والمذهب ظاهر الرواية.

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for proving the moon of Eid al-Adha. The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwaya) is that it is like the moon of Shawwal: when the sky is cloudy, it requires two male witnesses or one male and two females; when the sky is clear, a large crowd is needed. This is because many people benefit from the sacrificial meat, so stricter proof is required to avoid doubt. There is a rare transmission (nawadir) from Abu Hanifa that it is like the moon of Ramadan, where one witness suffices. However, the madhhab follows the apparent narration, which treats it like Shawwal.

Key Terms

نصاب الشهادة (niṣāb al-shahādah): The required number and qualification of witnesses for a particular type of testimony.
الجمع العظيم (al-jamʿ al-ʿaẓīm): A large, overwhelming crowd that provides certainty of the sighting.

The Hanafi Position on Unity of Horizon (Matali') in Moon Sighting
Ruling that moon sighting in one locality with same horizon binds all people

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that moon sighting in one locality with a shared horizon binds all Muslims, and contrast it with the intra-Hanafi dissent (ikhtilaf al-matali').

Core Idea
A single moon sighting within a common horizon obligates all regions — the general command 'Fast upon its sighting' is not divided by longitude.

The hadith 'Fast upon its sighting' seems universal, but does it apply to all Muslims worldwide, or only to those who directly see the moon? The Hanafi majority says the command is general: if the moon is established in one region, all regions sharing the same horizon must follow. However, some Hanafi scholars, like the author of al-Tajrid, dissented, arguing by analogy to prayer times that each locality follows its own sighting. This lesson unpacks the proof, the counter-argument, and the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its scope
Identify the relied-upon position (mufta bihi): if the moon is sighted in a town, all people within the same horizon (matla' qutr) are bound to fast. This is 'zahir al-madhhab' and 'qawl akthar al-mashayikh'.
The scope is limited to regions sharing the same horizon — not the entire globe.
2
Identify the opposing intra-Hanafi view
Some scholars, such as the author of al-Tajrid, hold that the ruling depends on the difference of horizons (ikhtilaf al-matali'), so each region follows its own sighting.
This is a minority view within the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The primary proof is the hadith 'صوموا لرؤيته' — the imperative 'sūmū' indicates obligation, and 'li-ru'yatihi' ties the obligation to the occurrence of sighting. Since sighting is absolute (mutlaq al-ru'ya), it is a cause for all within the same horizon.
The Hanafi usul principle 'al-amr yufidu al-wujub' and 'umum al-khitab' are applied here.
4
Examine the opposing dalil
The opposing view uses qiyas: just as the sun setting in one place does not make Maghrib obligatory on another where it has not set, similarly, moon sighting in one place should not bind another where the moon has not been sighted.
The analogy is based on the idea that the cause (sighting) is not universally present.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence: under unity of horizon, if one city fasts 30 days by sighting and another fasts 29, the latter must make up a day. Under ikhtilaf al-matali', no make-up is required. The mufta bihi is unity of horizon, being the cautious position.
The tarjih is based on the generality of the command and the precaution (ihtiyat) in worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وإذا ثبت الهلال (في) بلدة و (مطلـع قـطـر ) هـا (1) الزم سائر الناس في ظاهر المذهب، وعليه الفتوى) وهو قول (أكثر المشايخ)، حتى إذا صام أهــل بـلـدة ثلاثين بالرؤيا، وأهل بلدة تسعة وعشرين يوماً يجب عليهم قضاء يوم، لـعـمـوم الخطاب في قوله : صُومُوا لِرُؤْيَتِهِ » (۳) متعلقاً بمطلق الرؤية، وهي حاصلة برؤية قوم، فثبت بعموم الحكم احتياطاً، وقيل: تختلف ثبوته باختلاف المطالع واختاره، صاحب ( التجريد وغيره، كما إذا زالت الشمس عند قوم وغربت عند غيرهم، فالظهر على الأولين لا المغرب، لعدم انعقاد السبب في حقهم. تنبيه: لو صام أهل مصر بلا رؤية ثمانية وعشرين، فرأوا هلال شوال، إن أكملوا عدة شعبان عن رؤية هلاله قضوا يوماً واحداً؛ حملا على نقصان شعبان، وإن أكملوا شعبان لا عن رؤية هلاله، قضوا
And when the moon is established in a town and its horizon (of a region), it binds all the people in the apparent madhhab, and upon it is the fatwa, and it is the statement of most of the mashayikh. So much so that if the people of one town fast thirty days by sighting, and the people of another town fast twenty-nine days, they must make up one day, because of the generality of the address in His statement: 'Fast upon its sighting,' which is related to absolute sighting, and it is achieved by the sighting of a group, so the ruling is established generally as a precaution. And it was said that its establishment differs by the difference of the horizons, and the author of al-Tajrid and others chose that, like when the sun sets for some people and not for others, so Zuhr is upon the first group but not Maghrib, because the cause has not occurred in their right. A note: If the people of a city fasted twenty-eight days without a sighting, then they see the Shawwal moon, if they had completed the count of Sha'ban based on a sighting of its moon, they make up one day, attributing it to the deficiency of Sha'ban; and if they completed Sha'ban not based on a sighting of its moon, they make up...
Source pages p. 637

Commentary
This passage discusses whether the sighting of the moon in one place obligates all other regions to follow. The relied-upon position (zahir al-madhhab) is that if the moon is sighted in a region that shares the same horizon (matali'), all people must follow that sighting. For example, if one city fasts 30 days by sighting and another city fasts only 29, those who fasted 29 must make up a day because the sighting of the first city is binding. This is based on the general address of the hadith 'Fast upon its sighting' (صوموا لرؤيته), which is addressed to all Muslims. However, some scholars, like the author of al-Tajrid, hold that each region follows its own sighting because the cause (sighting) is not necessarily present for all. They analogize to the difference in prayer times due to different sun positions. The passage also includes a note about a scenario where a city fasts 28 days without any sighting and then sees the moon; they must make up days accordingly.

Key Terms
مطلع قطر (maṭlaʿ qutr): The same horizon or region where the moon rises at the same time.
اختلاف المطالع (ikhtilāf al-maṭāliʿ): The difference in the times of moon sighting due to geographical longitude; the view that each region follows its own sighting.
عموم الخطاب (ʿumūm al-khiṭāb): The generality of the address or command that applies to all Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) The ruling depends on the school of the second town's judge.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that moon sighting within a common horizon binds all regions; the general command of the hadith overrides the analogy to prayer times.

Ruling on Hilal of Eid al-Adha: Two Witnesses Required – Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Statement of ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute and tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on the testimony required for the crescent of Eid al-Adha and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the Narration of the Nawadir.

Core Idea
The crescent of Eid al-Adha requires two witnesses or a great multitude, unlike Ramadan which can accept one witness.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on proving the crescent for Eid al-Adha. The matn states it is like Eid al-Fitr, requiring the same standard of testimony. We will see why the Zahir al-Riwayah takes this position and how it differs from a rare narration attributed to Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key ruling in the matn
The matn states: 'وهلال الأضحى كالفطر' – the crescent of al-Adha is like al-Fitr. This means the same conditions for testimony apply: two just witnesses or a great multitude when the sky is clear.
Note the phrase 'كالفطر' – the analogy is to Eid al-Fitr, not Ramadan.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
The commentary reveals that there is a narration from Abu Hanifa (in al-Nawadir) that considers the crescent of al-Adha like that of Ramadan, where one witness suffices in cloudy conditions. This is a weaker, non-reliable position.
This dispute is between the Zahir al-Riwayah (the relied-upon corpus) and a rare narration (Nawadir).
3
Analyze the evidence for the Zahir al-Riwayah
The commentator argues that the benefit (maslaha) of the meat of sacrifices requires greater caution, hence stricter testimony is needed. The public interest demands a higher standard of proof.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) based on maslaha.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under the mufta bihi, if only one witness appears on a clear night, the crescent is not proven and the next day is not Eid. Under the Nawadir view, it would be accepted. This affects when the community performs the sacrifice.
The practical consequence is whether Eid is observed or deferred.
5
Identify the tarjih mechanism
The commentator declares the apparent riwaya as al-ashah (most correct) and mufta bihi, preferring it over the Nawadir narration because it is more cautious and serves the public benefit.
Tarjih is based on the strength of the transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) and the rational consideration of maslaha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(وهلالُ الأضحى) في الحكم (كالفطر) فلابد من نصاب الشهادة مع العلة، والجمع العظيــم مــع الصحو، علـى ظاهر الرواية، وهو الأصح لما تعلق به من نفع العباد بلحوم الأضاحي، خلافاً لما يروى عن أبي حنيفة أنه كهلال رمضان، وهي رواية ( النوادر ) وصححها في «التحفة» والمذهب ظاهر الرواية.
And the crescent of al-Adha is like al-Fitr. And it is required for the remaining crescents the testimony of two just men, or a free man and two free women, not hadd-punished for slander. And when it is established in the rising place of a region, it binds all the people, in the apparent madhhab, and upon it is the fatwa and most of the mashayikh. Source pages p. 637

Commentary
This passage begins by restating the matn: the crescent for Eid al-Adha is like that for Eid al-Fitr, meaning it requires two witnesses as a condition. The commentary explains that the relied-upon position in the madhhab requires either the standard two-witness testimony or a large multitude when the sky is clear. This is the apparent riwaya and the most correct view, contrary to a narration from Abu Hanifa (in al-Nawadir) that it is like the crescent of Ramadan (which only requires one witness in cloudy conditions). The commentator then discusses a complex intra-Hanafi dispute about the case where a community fasts thirty days without sighting: when should they break? The narration from al-Hasan (from Abu Hanifa) holds that they do not break fast out of caution, while Muhammad says they do break. Shaykh Akmal al-Din clarifies that this applies only when the sky is clear and they have not seen it; if cloudy, there is no need for this measure. The final verification is that the relied-upon position is the one stated in the text: the crescent of al-Adha requires the same testimony as al-Fitr, with the great multitude suffice in clear conditions.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The transmitted and relied-upon ruling from the core books of the school, distinguished from rare narrations (Nawadir).
النوادر (al-Nawadir): Rare or isolated narrations that are not part of the standard transmitted corpus of the school.
شهادة الواحد (shahadat al-wahid): Testimony of a single witness, which in some cases may be accepted for the crescent of Ramadan in cloudy conditions, but not for al-Adha according to the reliable position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The crescent of Eid al-Adha requires two witnesses or a great multitude in clear conditions; the rare narration allowing one witness is not relied upon for fatwa.

Witnesses for Non-Ramadan Crescents
Condition of witnesses for proving the crescent for months other than Ramadan and the two Eids.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the witness requirements for proving the crescent of any month other than Ramadan and the two Eids, and explain the binding effect of a sighting within a matla' qutr.

Core Idea
For non-Ramadan crescents: two just men or one man and two women.

This lesson extracts a clear ruling from the matn: the standard testimony requirements for establishing the beginning of a month other than Ramadan and the two Eids. It also clarifies that once the crescent is proven in a locality with a common horizon (matla' qutr), it becomes binding upon all residents of that region. This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
The act is 'proving the crescent' (thubut al-hilal) for months other than Ramadan and the two Eids. This is a condition for the obligation of fasting or celebrating Eid.
2
State the witness requirement
The matn requires two just men (rajulayn 'adlayn) OR one free man and two free women (hurr wa hurratayn). The witnesses must not have been flogged for qadhf (false accusation of zina).
Note the Hanafi distinction: for Ramadan, one witness suffices in cloud, but here standard testimony rules apply.
3
Understand the binding effect
If the crescent is established in one locality within a common horizon region (matla' qutr), it becomes binding on all people in that region. This is the apparent madhhab and relied-upon fatwa.
This prevents disputes within a shared horizon area.
4
Memorize the ruling
Commit to memory: 'Two just men or one man and two women; not hadd-punished for qadhf; proven in matla' qutr binds all.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويشترط لبقية الأهلة شهادة رجلين عدلين أو حر وحريتين غير محدودين في قذف. وإذا ثبت في مطلع قطر لزم سائر الناس في ظاهر المذهب وعليه الفتوى وأكثر المشايخ.
And it is required for the rest of the crescents the testimony of two just men, or a free man and two free women, not hadd-punished for slander. And when it is established in the rising point of a region, it binds all the people, in the apparent madhhab, and upon it is the fatwa and most of the mashayikh.
Source pages p. 637

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn: For proving the crescent of any month other than Ramadan and the two Eids, the standard two-witness rule applies. The witnesses must be just and not previously punished for false accusation of zina (qadhf). Alternatively, one free man and two free women suffice, similar to the general rule in Islamic testimony. The second part of the statement adds that if the crescent is proven in a locality with a common horizon (matla' qutr), it becomes binding on all people in that region. This is the relied-upon position, as held by most mashayikh.

Key Terms
مطلع قطر (matla' qutr): A region whose horizon is the same for moon sighting, generally considered the same time zone or area of similar latitude.
غير محدودين في قذف (ghayr mahdudayn fi qadhf): Witnesses must not have been flogged for false accusation of zina; such a flogging disqualifies them from ever testifying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Two just men
C) One man and one woman
D) One man and two women

Key Takeaway
For non-Ramadan crescents, two just men or one man plus two women (not qadhf-punished) are required; proven in a region binds all with a common horizon.

8 min
Binding Nature of Crescent Sighting in Common Horizon
Ruling that a proven sighting in one town binds all towns sharing the same rising point.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a crescent sighting in one locality binds all people sharing the same rising point, and explain the evidence from the general command 'Fast upon its sighting'.

Core Idea
A proven sighting of the moon in one region binds all who share its rising point — the command 'Fast upon its sighting' is general.

The crescent moon marks the beginning and end of Ramadan as a community obligation. But what if the moon is sighted in one town but not in another that lies within the same horizon? This passage from Nur al-Idah presents the relied-upon Hanafi position: the sighting is binding on all who share the same rising point (matla' qutr). We will examine the evidence from the hadith, the reasoning behind the majority view, and the minority intra-Hanafi opinion that differs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the sighting of the crescent (ru'yah al-hilal). The ruling is that when the sighting is established in one matla' (rising point), it becomes binding on all people in that region.
The ruling is wajib: the duty to fast is established for all.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The passage cites the Prophetic command 'صوموا لرؤيته' (Fast upon its sighting). This is a general address (khitab 'amm).
The hadith is ahad but accepted in practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
The command is attached to 'sighting' (ru'yatihi) in an absolute sense (mutlaq). Since the sighting occurs by a group of people, the ruling applies universally to all Muslims, not just those who saw the moon.
The generality of the lafz (صوموا) supports the binding nature.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
Some Hanafis (e.g., author of al-Tajrid) hold that sighting differs by location, analogous to prayer times—if the sun sets in one place, it does not obligate Maghrib elsewhere. Similarly, the crescent sighting may not bind distant towns.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference; Shafi'is generally also do not bind distant regions.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The text states that the relied-upon view is the binding view, and it is the fatwa. The reasoning includes precaution (ihtiyat) and adherence to the apparent generality of the command.
The mufta bihi is that all in the same matla' must fast if the moon is sighted there.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبت الهلال في مطلع قطر لزم سائر الناس في ظاهر المذهب وعليه الفتوى وهو قول أكثر المشايخ حتى إذا صام أهل بلدة ثلاثين بالرؤيا وأهل بلدة تسعة وعشرين يوماً يجب عليهم قضاء يوم لعموم الخطاب في قوله: صوموا لرؤيته متعلقاً بمطلق الرؤية وهي حاصلة برؤية قوم فثبت بعموم الحكم احتياطاً. وقيل: تختلف ثبوته باختلاف المطالع واختاره صاحب التجريد وغيره كما إذا زالت الشمس عند قوم وغربت عند غيرهم فالظهر على الأولين لا المغرب لعدم انعقاد السبب في حقهم.
And when the crescent is established in a rising point of a region, it binds all the people in the apparent madhhab, and upon it is the fatwa, and it is the statement of most of the mashayikh. So that if the people of a town fast thirty days by sighting and the people of another town fast twenty-nine days, they must make up a day, due to the generality of the address in His saying: 'Fast upon its sighting', being attached to absolute sighting, and it occurs by the sighting of a people, so it is established by the generality of the ruling out of precaution. And it is said: its confirmation differs according to the rising points, and the author of al-Tajrid and others chose it, just as when the sun sets for some people and rises for others, then Dhuhr is obligatory for the first, not Maghrib, because the cause is not established in their right.
Source pages p. 637

Commentary
The passage explains the ruling that when the crescent is proven in one location (sharing a common lunar horizon or matla' qutr), it becomes binding on all people in that region. This is the relied-upon position of the majority, based on the general command 'Fast upon its sighting' (hadith), which is interpreted to apply to any sighting anywhere. Consequently, if one town fasts a full thirty days based on sighting, and another related town only fasts twenty-nine (having not seen the moon), the second town must make up one day. However, there is an alternative view held by the author of al-Tajrid and others: that crescent sighting varies by location, just like the times of prayer differ. For example, if the sun sets in one place but not in another, the prayer times differ accordingly. But the mufta bihi is the first view, out of precaution.

Key Terms
مطلع قطر (matla' qutr): The rising place of the moon for a particular region; same as being in the same approximate longitude/latitude.
عموم الحكم (umum al-hukm): The generality of the ruling: the hadith's command applies to all Muslims universally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if the crescent is sighted in Makkah, is it binding upon people in Madinah if the two cities are considered to share the same horizon?
A) Yes, binding
B) No, each city has its own rising point
C) Only if Madinah also sees it
D) Binding only for Ramadan

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position: a proven sighting of the moon in one region (matla') binds all people in that region due to the general command 'Fast upon its sighting'.

Making Up Days When Fasting 28 Days Without Sighting
Ruling on makeup days based on confirmation of Shaban.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on how many days must be made up when a community fasts 28 days without sighting the Shawwal crescent, and identify the condition that changes the required number.

Core Idea
Precaution (ihtiyat) determines makeup days: one day if Shaban was sighted, two if counted.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah addresses a practical scenario: a community has fasted 28 days based on an assumption that Ramadan has started, but then the Shawwal crescent is sighted. The number of days they must make up depends on whether the previous month (Shaban) was confirmed by actual sighting or by completing 30 days. The ruling applies the principle of ihtiyat (precaution) to ensure no wajib fast is missed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
The community fasts 28 days without having sighted the Shawwal crescent. Then they see it. The month is incomplete; some days were missed.
The act of fasting is assumed to be for Ramadan, but the actual start of Ramadan is uncertain.
2
Distinguish the two subcases
Case 1: They completed the previous month (Shaban) by relying on a sighting of its crescent. Case 2: They completed Shaban without a sighting (i.e., by counting 30 days).
This affects how many days of Ramadan they actually fasted.
3
Apply the ruling for each case
In Case 1, they make up one day because the shortage is attributed to Ramadan being 29 days (Shaban was correctly 29 or 30). In Case 2, they make up two days because Shaban could have been 29, meaning they started Ramadan a day early, causing a potential shortage of two days.
The reasoning is based on the possibility of deficiency in the earlier months.
4
Understand the basis: ihtiyat (precaution)
The ruling is built on caution to ensure all obligatory fasts are completed. Since the actual beginning of Ramadan is uncertain, the makeup days cover the most likely shortfall.
Hanafis frequently apply ihtiyat in acts of worship to avoid missing a wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه: لو صام أهل مصر بلا رؤية ثمانية وعشرين، فرأوا هلال شوال، إن أكملوا عدة شعبان عن رؤية هلاله قضوا يوماً واحداً؛ حملا على نقصان شعبان، وإن أكملوا شعبان لا عن رؤية هلاله، قضوا يومين احتياطاً؛ لاحتمال نقصان شعبان مع ما قبله، فإنهم لما لم يروا هلال شعبان كانوا بالضرورة مكملين رجب. كذا في «الفتح».
Notification: If the people of a city fasted twenty-eight without sighting, and then they saw the crescent of Shawwal: if they completed the number of Shaban based on sighting its crescent, they make up one day; considering it as a deficiency of Shaban. And if they completed Shaban without sighting its crescent, they make up two days out of precaution; due to the possibility of deficiency of Shaban with what is before it, for since they did not see the crescent of Shaban, they were necessarily completing Rajab. Thus in al-Fath.
Source pages p. 637

Commentary
This tanbih deals with a scenario where a community fasts 28 days of Ramadan without having sighted the Shawwal crescent, and then they see it. The number of days they need to make up depends on whether they had a valid sighting for the previous month (Shaban). If they began Ramadan based on a sighting (so Shaban was set to 29 or 30), then the 28 days can only be possibly short by one day (since Shaban may have been 29, making Ramadan 29? Actually, if they fasted 28 and saw Shawwal, they have not completed Ramadan. If they had a proper sighting of Shaban, they would have started on 1 Ramadan, so 28 days means they are short by one day? Let's analyze: they fasted 28 after a proper sighting of Shaban; then if they see Shawwal on the 29th day of fasting? The text says they saw Hilal Shawwal after 28 days of fasting. So they must have started Ramadan after a proper Shaban sighting; then Ramadan would have 30 days if they saw Shawwal after 28? Actually, clarify: They started Ramadan based on sighting of Shaban. They fasted 28 days then saw Shawwal. That means they have only fasted 28 days of Ramadan, but the sighting of Shawwal indicates that the 29th day is Eid. So Ramadan was only 29 days? They need to make up one day for the missing fast. If they had no proper sighting for Shaban (completed it to 30 by counting), then they might have started a day early or late? The text says if they completed Shaban without sighting, they make up two days. This is because there is a possibility that Shaban was short (29) and they may have started a day earlier, making their Ramadan start on a wrong day, so the shortfall could be two days. The commentator refers to al-Fath.

Key Terms
احتياطاً (ihtiyatan): Out of precaution; the ruling is based on caution to ensure the fasts are complete.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a community fasts 28 days without sighting and then sees the Shawwal crescent, and they had completed Shaban based on sighting its crescent, how many days must they make up?
A) None
B) One day
C) Two days
D) Twenty-nine days

Key Takeaway
The number of makeup days depends on how the previous month was confirmed: one day if by sighting, two if by counting, due to precaution.

Daytime Sighting of Crescent Belongs to Coming Night
Ruling that a daytime sighting is not considered; it belongs to the next night.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on daytime crescent sighting and distinguish the positions of al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and Abu Yusuf from the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
A daytime crescent sighting is not valid for the new month; it belongs to the coming night.

In the Hanafi school, the sighting of the new moon must occur after sunset to be valid for the new month. A sighting during the day — even before noon — is disregarded for the current night. However, within the madhhab, there are nuanced positions from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and Abu Yusuf. This lesson clarifies the relied-upon ruling and the basis of the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The matn states that daytime sighting is not considered, whether before or after noon. The selected view attributes it to the coming night.
No consideration means it does not establish the new month for the current night.
2
Analyze al-Hasan ibn Ziyad's distinction
He differentiates based on whether the moon sets before or after twilight (shafaq). If before, it belongs to the past night; if after, to the next.
This uses the marker of sunset vs. twilight to determine the moon's age.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's position
He considers a pre-noon sighting for the past night in matters of fasting and breaking fast.
The text refers to al-Burhan for this view.
4
Determine the tarjih
The mufta bihi is the selected view that it is always for the coming night, regardless of timing or moonset.
The text explicitly says 'في المختار' (in the selected view).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا عبرة برؤية الهلال نهاراً، سواءً كان قبلَ الزَّوالِ أو بعده، وهو الليلةُ المُسْتَقْبَلَةُ في المختار. قال « الحسن بن زياد » : إن غاب قبل الشفق فللماضية، وإن غاب بعده فللقابلة، ويجعل أبو يوسف الهلال المرئي قبل الزوال للماضية في الصوم والفطر، كما في « البرهان»، والله أعلم.
And no consideration is given to seeing the crescent during the day, whether it is before noon or after, and it is for the coming night in the selected (view). Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad said: If it sets before the twilight, it is for the past night; if after twilight, for the next night. And Abu Yusuf makes the crescent seen before noon for the past night in fasting and breaking fast, as in al-Burhan, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 638

Commentary
The matn states that a sighting of the crescent during daylight hours is not valid for establishing the new month. In the relied-upon view (al-mukhtar), that sighting is attributed to the coming night, not the past night. For example, if someone sees the moon on the morning of the 30th, it does not mean that tonight is already the first of the next month; instead, that moon is considered the leading edge of the next month, so the new month begins after sunset. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad distinguishes based on whether the moon sets before or after the twilight (shafaq). If before, then it was likely the old moon (for the past night), and the day is part of the old month; if after, it is the new moon. Abu Yusuf limits the disagreement: he considers a pre-noon sighting as belonging to the past night for purposes of fasting and breaking fast (i.e., if seen before noon, it counts for the night just ended, so they would have completed the month, and that day is already Eid? Actually, the text is brief. The commentator may be relying on more detail but this is what is here.

Key Terms
الشفق (al-shafaq): The twilight after sunset; used by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad as a marker for the moon's age.
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen or relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school, if someone sees the crescent of Shawwal at 10:00 AM on the 30th day of Ramadan, what is the ruling?
A) That day is Eid
B) The fast is still valid for that day
C) They must break fast immediately
D) The month was already completed

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a daytime crescent sighting is always attributed to the coming night, regardless of whether it occurs before or after noon, and regardless of the time of moonset.

The Legal Stratagem (Hila) for Proving the Crescent of Ramadan
Explains a legal stratagem for proving the crescent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions of the hila for proving the crescent and explain why direct judicial ruling on the month is not required.

Core Idea
Use a conditional debt claim to make a judge indirectly establish the month.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains a clever Hanafi workaround when one needs to prove the start of Ramadan in court. Since the judge cannot issue a ruling on a religious month directly, the scholars devised a stratagem: a conditional agency agreement for debt collection that forces the court to rule on a monetary issue, thereby establishing the month as a logical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Obstacle
Note that the passage states the crescent of Ramadan cannot be 'proven' by a judicial verdict (hukm) because it is a religious matter, not a legal dispute between parties.
The court only rules on disputes over rights (hukm), not on pure religious facts.
2
Understand the Hila Structure
The hila involves a conditional agency (wakala mu'allaqa): someone appoints an agent to collect a debt 'if Ramadan enters'. The debtor acknowledges the agency but denies Ramadan has entered.
The condition must be clear and possible.
3
Witness Testimony
Witnesses testify that Ramadan has entered (e.g., they saw the crescent). The judge then rules on the debt, implying the truth of the condition.
The judge does not 'decree' Ramadan; he decides the monetary case, and the month's arrival is a necessary consequence.
4
Alternative without Hila
The passage mentions that even without this device, if a reliable person reports the sighting (especially on a cloudy day), the judge may accept it and order fasting, but this is not a formal judicial proof.
This shows the flexible approach: the judge can act on information without a formal trial.
5
Key Principle
The underlying rule: the start of Ramadan is established by sighting or completing Sha'ban, not by court judgment. The hila is just a practical tool to get a judicial record.
Fasting obligation depends on actual knowledge, not on a judge's ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه آخر في كيفية إثبات الهلال الوجه في إثبات الرمضانية والعيد، أن يدعي عند القاضي بوكالة رجل معلقة بدخول رمضان بقبض دين، فيقر الخصم بالوكالة وينكر دخول رمضان، فيشهد الشهود بذلك فيقضي عليه بالمال فيثبت مجيء رمضان؛ لأن إثبات مجيء رمضان لا يدخل تحت الحكم، حتى لو أخبر رجل عدل القاضي بمجيء رمضان يقبل لغيم ونحوه، ويأمر الناس بالصوم، قال في « الكافي» : ويصام برؤية الهلال [ وإكمال شعبان؛ لأن الصوم لا يتوقف على الثبوت ولا يلزم من رؤيته ثبوته ] كذا في « البحر».
Another notification regarding the method of proving the crescent. The valid way to prove the arrival of Ramadan and Eid is that a person claims before the judge by an agency (wakala) of a man conditioned on the entry of Ramadan for collecting a debt. The opponent acknowledges the agency but denies the entry of Ramadan. Then the witnesses testify to that, and the judge decides for the money, thus establishing the arrival of Ramadan, because the establishment of the arrival of Ramadan is not subject to legal judgment. So that if a just man reports to the judge the arrival of Ramadan for cloudiness or the like, he accepts it and orders the people to fast. He said in al-Kafi: And one fasts by sighting the crescent and completing Shaban, because fasting is not dependent on judicial confirmation, and its sighting does not necessitate its establishment. Thus in al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 638

Commentary
This tanbih explains a legal stratagem (hila) to have the crescent of Ramadan or Eid formally proven in a judicial setting. Since the court cannot directly 'prove' the start of Ramadan because it is not a legal matter (but a religious determination that does not require a judge's ruling), one can achieve the same result indirectly. For instance, someone appointed another as agent to collect a debt conditional upon Ramadan entering. If the debtor admits the agency but denies Ramadan has entered, and the witnesses testify to the sighting, the judge can rule on the debt (which is a legal ruling) and thereby the fact of Ramadan's entry becomes established as a necessary consequence. The judge then can order people to fast. The passage also notes that even without such a hila, if a reliable person reports the sighting (even one witness in cloudy condition), the judge may inform people, but it is not a binding legal proof in the same way.

Key Terms
وكالة معلقة (wakala mu'allaqa): An agency that is conditional upon a future event (e.g., the entry of Ramadan).
حيلة شرعية (hila shar'iyyah): A legal stratagem that achieves a permissible goal by lawful means.
لا يدخل تحت الحكم (la yadkhulu tahta al-hukm): It is not subject to judicial ruling or decree.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the hila is needed to prove the crescent in court?
A) The judge cannot issue a ruling on religious matters like the start of Ramadan.
B) Witnesses are not available.
C) The debtor refuses to pay.
D) The agency contract is invalid.

Key Takeaway
You can prove the crescent indirectly through a conditional debt lawsuit, because the court can’t rule on a religious fact directly, but can rule on money.

Great Multitude Testimony Does Not Require Islam
Ruling that a great multitude's testimony is accepted regardless of religion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the testimony of a great multitude is accepted even if the witnesses are non-Muslim, and explain the basis in tawatur.

Core Idea
A multitude reaching tawatur makes the faith of individuals irrelevant.

This tanbih from Nur al-Idah addresses a practical concern: when a huge crowd reports seeing the crescent, do we need each witness to be Muslim? The Hanafi answer is no, because their number eliminates the possibility of collusion. This lesson anchors that rule and its underlying usul concept.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Learn the exact rule: Islam is not a condition for accepting the report of a great multitude. Write it down.
Focus on the phrase 'jamm' 'adhim' and 'mutawatir'.
2
Identify the reason
Understand why: because their report reaches tawatur, which gives certainty. Tawatur overrides individual reliability.
Tawatur means so many narrators that lying is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه آخر مهم لا يشترط الإسلام في إخبار الجمع العظيم؛ لأن المتواتر لا يبالي فيه بكفر الناقلين فضلاً عن فسقهم أو ضعفهم، كما ذكره الكمال عند قوله فصل في كيفية القطع
Another important notification: Islam is not required in the report of a great multitude, because the mutawatir (mass-transmitted report) does not care about the disbelief of the narrators, let alone their sinfulness or weakness, as al-Kamal mentioned at his saying: Chapter on the method of certainty.
Source pages p. 638

Commentary
This brief tanbih states that when a very large number of people (jamma' 'azhim) reports seeing the crescent, it is accepted even if they are not Muslims. The reason is that their report reaches the level of tawatur (indubitable mass transmission), where the high number makes it impossible for them to all have conspired to lie. This applies to the crescent sighting: if an overwhelmingly large crowd reports it, their report is accepted regardless of their religious status or personal integrity. The commentator references al-Kamal (Ibn al-Humam?) in his discussion on qat' (certainty).

Key Terms
جمع عظيم (jamm' 'adhim): A very large multitude whose report is considered mutawatir, thus requiring no scrutiny of individuals.
متواتر (mutawatir): A report transmitted by such a large number that it is impossible they conspired to lie.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When each individual is just
B) When the number reaches tawatur
C) When they are all from the same tribe
D) When the sky is cloudy

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts the testimony of a great multitude for crescent sighting even if they are non-Muslim, because the number ensures tawatur.

Daytime Crescent Sighting: Coming or Past Night?
Ruling on daytime crescent sighting and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on daytime crescent sighting and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad from Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A crescent seen by day belongs to the coming night, not the past.

When you see the new moon crescent during daylight hours, which night does it announce? This passage from Imdad al-Fattah addresses that very question. The relied-upon Hanafi position assigns it to the coming night, but there is an important intra-Hanafi difference. Understanding this ruling prevents confusion in starting Ramadan or Eid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states: 'And no consideration is given to seeing the crescent during the daytime, whether before or after noon, and it is for the coming night in the chosen opinion.' State the ruling clearly: a daytime sighting indicates the coming night.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that a pre-noon sighting is for the past night. Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad distinguishes by whether the crescent sets before or after twilight. Identify these alternative positions.
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's view is the mufta bihi.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
The text cites the hadith: 'Fast for its sighting and break fast for its sighting.' The Hanafi interpretation is that the sighting must precede the fast, and the implied meaning is sighting at evening of the last day. Therefore, a daytime sighting cannot announce the past night.
This is a dalil naqli (textual evidence).
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Apply the difference: If the crescent is seen before noon on 30th Sha'ban, Abu Hanifa says the coming night is Ramadan's first, while Abu Yusuf says it is still Sha'ban. The practice consequence is the start of fasting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا عبرة برؤية الهلالِ نهاراً، سواءً كان قبلَ الزَّوالِ أو بعده، وهو الليلةُ المُسْتَقْبَلَةُ في المختار. احتياطاً؛ لاحتمال نقصان شعبان مع ما قبله، فإنهم لما لم يروا هلال شعبان كانوا بالضرورة مکملین رجب. كذا في «الفتح». تنبيه آخر في كيفية إثبات الهلال الوجه في إثبات الرمضانية والعيد، أن يدعي عند القاضي بوكالة رجل معلقة بدخول رمضان بقبض دين، فيقر الخصم بالوكالة وينكر دخول رمضان، فيشهد الشهود بذلك فيقضي عليه بالمال فيثبت مجيء رمضان؛ لأن إثبات مجيء رمضان لا يدخل تحت الحكم، حتى لو أخبر رجل عدل القاضي بمجيء رمضان يقبل لغيم ونحوه، ويأمر النـاس بـالصوم، قال في ( الكافي» : ويصام برؤية الهلال [ وإكمال شعبان؛ لأن الصوم لا يتوقف على الثبوت ولا يلزم من رؤيته ثبوته ] كذا في « البحر». تنبیه آخر مهم لا يشترط الإسلام في إخبار الجمع العظيم؛ لأن المتواتــر لا يـبـالـي فـيـه بـكـفـر الناقلين فضلاً عن فسقهم أو ضعفهم، كما ذكره الكمال عند قوله فصل في كيفية القطع (ولا عبرة برؤية الهلال نهاراً، سواء كان قد رؤي (قبلَ الزَّوال أو بعده، وهو الليلةُ المُسْتَقْبَلَةُ) عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد، وهو قول ابن مسعود وأنس، ورواية أخرى عن عمر لقوله : « صُومُوا لِرُؤْيَتِهِ وَأَفْطِرُوا لِرُؤيَتِهِ ) () فوجب سبق الرؤية على الصوم والفطر، والمفهوم المتبادر منه الرؤية عند عشية آخر كــل شهر عند الصحابة والتابعين ومن بعدهم وذلك (في المختار) من المذهب، وعن أبي حنيفة: إن كان مجراه أمام الشمس وهي تتلوه فهو للماضية، وإن كان خلفها فللمستقبلة. قال « الحسن بن زياد » : إن غاب قبل الشفق فللماضية، وإن غاب بعده فللقابلة، ويجعل أبو يوسف الهلال المرئي قبل الزوال للماضية في الصوم والفطر، كما في « البرهان»، والله أعلم.
And no consideration is given to seeing the crescent during the daytime, whether it was seen before noon or after, and it is for the coming night in the chosen opinion. As a precaution due to the possibility of Sha'ban being incomplete with what preceded it, for when they did not see the crescent of Sha'ban they necessarily completed Rajab. Thus in al-Fath. Another note on the method of proving the crescent: The face of proving Ramadan and Eid is that a person claims before the judge by a conditional agency for collecting a debt, then the opponent admits the agency but denies Ramadan, then witnesses testify to that, so the judge rules for the debt, thereby establishing the advent of Ramadan because proving Ramadan does not fall under judicial ruling. So if a just man informs the judge of Ramadan, it is accepted due to clouds etc., and he orders people to fast. It is said in al-Kafi: Fasting is with sighting the crescent and completing Sha'ban, because fasting does not depend on proof nor does sighting necessitate its proof. Thus in al-Bahr. Another important note: Islam is not a condition for the report of a large multitude, because mutawatir is not affected by the disbelief of transmitters, let alone their sin or weakness, as al-Kamal mentioned at his statement 'Section on the manner of cutting'. And no consideration is given to seeing the crescent during the daytime, whether it was seen before noon or after, and it is for the coming night according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and it is the statement of Ibn Mas'ud and Anas, and another narration from Umar due to his statement: 'Fast for its sighting and break fast for its sighting.' So the sighting must precede the fast and breaking fast, and the implied understanding from it is the sighting at the evening of the last day of each month among the Companions and Successors and those after them, and that is the chosen position of the school. And from Abu Hanifa: If its course is in front of the sun and it follows it, it is for the past night, and if behind it, it is for the coming night. Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad said: If it sets before the twilight it is for the past night, and if after it, for the coming night. And Abu Yusuf makes the crescent seen before noon as for the past night in fasting and breaking fast, as in al-Burhan. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 638

Commentary
This passage from the commentary covers three related topics. First, it states the ruling that a crescent moon seen during the daytime is assigned to the coming night (the night of the following day). This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, taken as a precaution because if Sha'ban was incomplete, then the crescent belongs to the next month. Second, it explains a legal trick (hila) to prove the arrival of Ramadan without a direct judicial ruling: a person sues for a debt contingent on Ramadan, and when the opponent admits the agency but denies Ramadan, witnesses testify to the sighting, and the judge rules for payment, thereby indirectly establishing Ramadan. Third, it notes that for a very large crowd (tawatur), the reporters need not be Muslim, as tawatur eliminates the need for individual reliability. The passage then returns to the crescent dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that a daytime sighting is for the coming night, supported by hadith and early practice. Abu Hanifa also distinguished based on the crescent's position relative to the sun. Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad distinguished based on whether the crescent sets before or after twilight. Abu Yusuf, however, considers a pre-noon sighting as for the past night. The chosen position (mukhtar) is for the coming night.

Key Terms
الهلال (al-hilāl): The new moon crescent; legally, the first appearance of the moon after conjunction, used to determine lunar months.
الليلة المستقبلة (al-layla al-mustaqbala): The coming night, i.e., the night following the daytime of sighting.
الليلة الماضية (al-layla al-māḍiya): The past night, i.e., the night preceding the daytime of sighting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if the crescent is seen at 10 AM on 30th Sha'ban, the coming night is the ___ of Ramadan.
A) 1st night
B) 30th night
C) 2nd night
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling: a daytime crescent sighting is for the coming night, based on the hadith 'Fast for its sighting' and the practice of the Companions.
