مِسْكِيناً؟ قال: لا، ثُمَّ جلس فَجِيء إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بَعَرَقٍ فِيهِ تَمْرٍ فَقَالَ: «تَصَدَّقْ بِهَذَا قَالَ: عَلَى أَفْقَرَ مِنَّا فَمَا بَيْنَ لا بَتيها أهلُ بيت أحوج إليهِ مِنَّا، فَضَحِكَ النَّبي صلى الله عليه وسلم حَتَّى بَدَتْ نَوَاجِدُهُ، وقال: «اذْهَبْ فَأَطْعِمْهُ أهْلَكَ» رواه الجماعة. وهذا ظـاهـر عـلـى وجوبه مرتباً، وخص الأعرابي بأحكام ثلاثة بجواز الإطعام مع القدرة على الصيام، وصرفه إلى نفسه، والاكتفاء بخمسة عشر صاعاً، كذا قاله الزيلعي، لأن العرق بالعين - مكتل - يسع خمس خمسة عشر صاعاً، والنواجذ أضراس الحلم الواحد ناجذ كذا في (المغرب) انتهى. قلت: إلا أن في قوله خصـه
(And the kaffarah is the freeing of a slave, even if she is not a believer, due to the absolute nature of the text concerning it, and its condition is that the benefits of strength, walking, speech, sight, and intellect are not lost, as in zihar. Then if he is unable to do that, i.e., freeing, because he does not possess a slave nor the price to buy one, he fasts two consecutive months in which there is no day of Eid, nor any day of the Days of Tashriq, due to the prohibition of fasting them. Then if he is unable to fast due to illness or old age, he feeds sixty poor persons, giving them a morning meal and an evening meal that are filling, or two morning meals, or two evening meals, or an evening meal and a pre-dawn meal, or he gives every poor person half a sa' of wheat, or its flour, or its grits, or a sa' of dates, or barley, or its value... or a poor person. And he only mentions 'miskin' to preserve what is mentioned in the text, although the condition is that they are not wealthy. And it is not required that all of them gather at one time. If they do gather, he gives them a morning meal and an evening meal that are filling, and this is the most just to fulfill the need of the day entirely. Or he gives them two morning meals from two days, or two evening meals from two nights, or an evening meal and a pre-dawn meal. And the condition is that those whom he feeds the second time must be the same as those he fed the first time; so if he feeds sixty in the morning and then feeds sixty others, it does not suffice until he repeats the feeding for one of the two groups. And if he feeds a single poor person for sixty days, it suffices him, because with the renewal of need, that poor person becomes like another poor person each day. And the condition, when the food is distributed, is that they are filled. Wheat bread suffices without any seasoning (udm), unlike barley bread, for which seasoning is necessary, because due to its coarseness, one cannot usually feel full without seasoning, whereas wheat bread has its seasoning within it, so it is said: wheat bread has its seasoning in it; whoever seeks seasoning for it is not hungry. And the condition is that none of them are full; if someone has eaten, he is like the hungry person in needing food for another (i.e., he should feed another). Or he gives every poor person half a sa' of wheat, or of its flour, or of its grits, i.e., from wheat, or he gives every poor person a sa' of dates, or a sa' of barley, or raisins, or he gives its value, i.e., the value of half a sa' of wheat or the value of a sa' of barley, even at different times. And that is due to the hadith of Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: A man came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and said, 'I am destroyed, O Messenger of Allah!' He said, 'What destroyed you?' He said, 'I had intercourse with my wife during Ramadan.' He said, 'Do you have what you can free a slave?' He said, 'No.' He said, 'Can you fast two consecutive months?' He said, 'No.' He said, 'Do you have what you can feed sixty poor persons?' He said, 'No.' Then he sat down, and a basket containing dates was brought to the Prophet (peace be upon him). He said, 'Give this in charity.' He said, 'To someone poorer than us? There is no family between its two lava plains who is more in need than us.' The Prophet (peace be upon him) laughed until his molars (nawajidh) appeared and said, 'Go and feed it to your family.' Narrated by the group. This is apparent upon its being obligatory in order, and he made three special rulings for the Bedouin: the permissibility of feeding even though he was able to fast, directing it to himself, and being satisfied with fifteen sa' (of dates). As az-Zayla'i said, because the basket ('araq) is a measure that holds fifteen sa'. And nawajidh are the molars of wisdom, singular: najidh, as in al-Mughrib, end. I say: except that in his saying 'he made him special'...
Source pages p. 651

Commentary
This passage details the three sequential options for kaffarah (expiation) for intentionally breaking a Ramadan fast. First, one must free a slave, even a non-Muslim slave, provided the slave has full physical and mental faculties (strength, vision, speech, intelligence). If unable (no slave or price), one must fast two consecutive months, excluding Eid days and the Days of Tashriq (11-13 Dhul Hijjah) because these are prohibited for fasting. If unable to fast due to illness or old age, one must feed sixty poor persons. The feeding can be done in various ways: by providing a filling morning and evening meal on the same day, or two morning meals, or two evening meals, or an evening meal and a pre-dawn meal (suhur). Alternatively, one may give each poor person half a sa' of wheat (or its flour or grits) or a full sa' of dates, barley, or raisins, or the monetary equivalent. It is not required to gather all sixty at once; one can feed a single poor person over sixty days. The food must be filling; bread made from wheat is sufficient without any side dish (udm) because it is inherently filling, whereas barley bread requires udm to be satisfying. The hadith of the Bedouin who had intercourse during Ramadan is cited as the primary proof for the sequence and the option of feeding. The hadith also shows special concessions for the poor: he was allowed to feed his own family with the dates meant for charity, and the feeding was considered sufficient with only fifteen sa' (the size of the basket), though the standard is sixty sa' (half sa' each for sixty). The commentary notes that az-Zayla'i said this hadith gives the Bedouin three special rulings, but the author adds a caution that these were specific to him.

Key Terms
تحرير رقبة (tahrir raqabah): Freeing a slave; the first option in kaffarah. The slave must have full physical and mental faculties.
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume; approximately 3.36 liters or 2.6 kg of wheat.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for a sin; specifically here for intentional break of a Ramadan fast.
متابعين (mutatabi'ayn): Consecutive; the two months of fasting must be uninterrupted except for prohibited days.
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah, days when fasting is prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum quantity of wheat to give to each of the sixty poor persons for kaffarah?
A) Half a sa' of wheat.
B) One sa' of wheat.
C) Two mudds of wheat.
D) A full meal once.

Key Takeaway
Kaffarah for intentional fast-breaking must be performed in the fixed sequence: free a slave, then fast two consecutive months, then feed sixty poor persons, with strict conditions for each step, as established by the hadith of the Bedouin.

Sawm — Fasting

Methods of Feeding Sixty Poor for Kaffarah
Details the allowed methods of feeding as expiation for breaking fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the valid methods of feeding sixty poor for kaffarah and apply the conditions for each method according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Feeding sixty poor for kaffarah can be done by meals or measured food, with specific conditions for validity.

When a person deliberately breaks a Ramadan fast, they must perform kaffarah. One of the options is feeding sixty poor people. But what does 'feeding' mean exactly? The Hanafi school provides detailed guidance on the methods, quantities, and conditions to ensure the expiation is valid. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains these rules with supporting evidence from the Prophet's hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that the act is fulfilling kaffarah by feeding sixty poor. The ruling is wajib (obligatory) after the inability to free a slave or fast two months.
Kaffarah is wajib, not fard, because its evidence is from ahad hadith (zanni al-thubut).
2
List the valid methods of feeding
From the passage, identify the different ways to feed: two filling meals (lunch and dinner), two lunches, two dinners, dinner and pre-dawn meal, or giving measured food (half sa' of wheat or equivalent, or a sa' of dates/barley/raisins/their value).
These methods are all acceptable.
3
Apply the conditions for validity
Check the conditions: if feeding multiple times, the same poor individuals must be fed each time (or one person over 60 days works); the food must be filling; wheat bread alone suffices, but barley needs a condiment; the poor must not be already full.
Feeding sixty different poor once is invalid.
4
Locate the dalil and analyze its wajh al-dalalah
The passage cites the hadith of the man who had intercourse in Ramadan. The Prophet offered the man the option to feed sixty poor after he could not free a slave or fast. This proves that feeding is a valid alternative, and the Prophet's practical demonstration (feeding his own family with a basket of dates) indicates the permissible quantities.
The imperative 'feed' implies obligation in order according to Hanafi usul.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and tarjih
The passage notes that the hadith shows the obligation is in order (slave, then fasting, then feeding). This is the Hanafi position. Some other schools (like Shafi'i) see the order as preferred but not obligatory. The Hanafi tarjih relies on the apparent order in the hadith.
The mufta bihi is the strict sequence.

(۱) انظر الحديث الآتي.
(۲) الصاع = ٤ أمداد = ٨ أرطال = ١٠٢٧,٥٧ درهماً = ٣,٣٦٢ لتراً = ٣٢٦١,٥ غراماً. معجم لغة الفقهاء / صاع /. (۳) أخرجه البخاري في الصيام، باب: إذا جامع في رمضان ولم يكن له شيء فتصدق عليه فليكفر (١٩٣٦)، ومسلم في الصوم، باب: تغليظ تحريم الجماع في نهار رمضان على الصائم، ووجوب الكفارة (۱۱۱۱).
He gives them lunch and dinner, two filling meals, or two lunches, or two dinners, or dinner and pre-dawn meal, or gives each poor person half a sa' of wheat, or its flour, or its fine flour, or a sa' of dates, or barley, or its value... or a poor person. He mentions the poor person in accordance with the text, although the condition is not being rich. It is not required that they all gather at one time. If they gather, he gives them lunch and dinner, two filling meals – this is the most equitable to cover the need of the day entirely. Or he gives them two lunches from two days, or two dinners from two nights, or dinner and pre-dawn meal, with the condition that those he fed the second time are the same as the first. If he fed sixty then fed a different sixty, it is not valid until he repeats the feeding for one group. If he fed one poor person for sixty days, it suffices because with renewed need, that poor person becomes like a different poor person each day. The condition when food is permissible is that it fills them. Wheat bread suffices without condiment, unlike barley which requires condiment because due to its coarseness, one cannot usually be filled except with condiment alongside barley bread. Hence it is said: wheat bread has its condiment in it; whoever seeks a condiment for it is not hungry. The condition is that none of them is full; if one is like a hungry person who has eaten, he still needs feeding. Or he gives each poor person half a sa' of wheat, or its flour, or its fine flour i.e. wheat, or gives each poor person a sa' of dates, or a sa' of barley or raisins, or gives its value i.e. the value of half a sa' of wheat or the value of a sa' of barley, even at separate times. This is based on the hadith of Abu Huraira that a man came to the Messenger of Allah and said: 'I am ruined, O Messenger of Allah.' He said: 'What ruined you?' He said: 'I had intercourse with my wife in Ramadan.' He said: 'Do you have what to free a slave?' He said: No. He said: 'Are you able to fast two consecutive months?' He said: No. He said: 'Do you have what to feed sixty poor?' He said: No. Then he sat down, and a basket of dates was brought to the Prophet, and he said: 'Give this in charity.' He said: 'To one poorer than us, there is no family between the two lava fields more needy than us.' So the Prophet laughed until his molars appeared and said: 'Go and feed it to your family.' Narrated by the group. This clearly shows its obligation in order, and the Bedouin was given three rulings: the permissibility of feeding despite ability to fast, spending it on himself, and sufficiency of fifteen sa'. Thus said al-Zayla'i because the basket (araq) holds fifteen sa'. And the nawajidh are the molars of puberty; one is najidh as in al-Mughrib. End. I say: except that in his statement 'especially...'
Source pages p. 652

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the method of fulfilling the kaffarah for breaking a Ramadan fast through feeding sixty poor people. It begins by listing the options: either provide two filling meals (lunch and dinner) to the poor, or provide two lunches or two dinners from separate days, or a dinner and a pre-dawn meal. The key condition is that the same poor individuals must be fed each time; if you feed a different group, it is invalid. However, feeding a single poor person for sixty consecutive days is acceptable because each day's need makes them like a different person. The food must be filling. Wheat bread alone suffices without any condiment, but barley bread requires a condiment because barley is coarse and not easily satiating without it. Another option is to give each poor person a measured quantity of staple food: half a sa' of wheat (or its flour or fine flour), or a full sa' of dates, barley, or raisins, or the monetary value thereof. The proof is the famous hadith of the man who had intercourse in Ramadan; the Prophet offered the options of freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor, and ultimately allowed the man to feed his own family with the dates. The commentary notes that the hadith implies the kaffarah is obligatory in order (slave then fasting then feeding), but the Bedouin was given special dispensations. This passage is typical of Hanafi fiqh: detailed conditions for each option, emphasis on practicality (e.g., spreading feeding over time), and reliance on prophetic hadith.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation required for deliberately invalidating the fast, consisting of freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor.
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume approximately 3.36 liters, used for determining the quantity of food given in kaffarah.
مسكين (miskin): A poor person in need, not necessarily the same as faqir; here used for recipient of kaffarah feeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Feeding sixty different poor people once each, without repeating any.
B) Feeding one poor person a filling meal for sixty consecutive days.
C) Giving each of sixty poor people a piece of bread no larger than a date.
D) Providing two dinners on the same night to two different groups of thirty.

Key Takeaway
Feeding sixty poor for kaffarah can be done via filling meals or measured food, with strict conditions on continuity and satiation, based on the prophetic hadith.

Sawm — Fasting

The Ruling of Tadakhul in Kaffarah for Repeated Fasting Violations
Ruling on tadakhul in kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tadakhul in kaffarah for repeated fasting violations and apply the conditions for when one kaffarah suffices.

Core Idea
One kaffarah suffices for multiple violations if no kaffarah intervened, even across different Ramadans.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah addresses a practical scenario: a person who intentionally breaks the fast multiple times (by intercourse or eating) on different days. The Hanafi school applies the principle of tadakhul (interference) to merge multiple expiations into one, provided no expiation has been performed in between. The underlying rationale is that kaffarah is intended as a deterrent, and a single expiation achieves that purpose. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its conditions, and the intra-madhhab discussion regarding violations spanning two Ramadans.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is multiple deliberate violations of the fast (intercourse or eating) on separate days. The ruling is that one kaffarah suffices for all such violations under specific conditions.
The ruling applies as long as no kaffarah has been performed between the violations.
2
Recognize the condition for tadakhul
The key condition is that no kaffarah has been performed between the violations. If a person commits a violation, then performs a kaffarah, then commits another violation, tadakhul does not apply; each violation requires its own kaffarah.
This is based on the principle that merging occurs before performance, not after, similar to hudud penalties.
3
Understand the scope of the condition
The condition applies even when violations occur in different Ramadans, according to the correct view (al-sahih). There is an alternative view (qil) that tadakhul only applies within one Ramadan.
The text explicitly says 'ala al-sahih' for including two Ramadans, indicating the preferred view.
4
Contrast with the case where kaffarah intervenes
If kaffarah does intervene between violations, one kaffarah does not suffice. This is the ruling in zahir al-riwayah, meaning it is the well-known transmitted position.
The principle is that tadakhul is only valid before the performance of the expiation, not after.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school generally does not accept tadakhul for kaffarah across multiple days, requiring a separate expiation for each violation. The Hanafi position is based on the purpose of kaffarah as deterrence, which is achieved by one expiation.
This difference arises from varying interpretations of the underlying rationale (illah) of kaffarah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكَفَتْ كفارةً واحدةً، عن جمَاعِ وأكل متعدد في أيامٍ، لم يَتَخَلَّلْهُ تكفير، ولو من رمضانَين، على الصحيح. فإِنْ تَخَلَّلَ التَّكْفِير لا تكفي كفارة واحدة، في ظاهر الرواية.
بالإطعام مع القدرة على الصيام تأمل، لأنه لما قال له: «هَلْ تَسْتَطِيعُ أَنْ تَصُومَ شَهْرَينِ مُتَتَابِعَين؟ قال: لا ) ( وكَفَتْ كفّارةً واحدةً عن جماع وأكل) عمداً (متعدد في أيام) كثيرة و (لم يَتَخَلَّلْهُ) أي: الجماع والأكل عمداً ( تكفير)؛ لأن الكفارة شرعت للزجر وهو يحصل بواحدة للتداخل، (ولــو) كـانت الأيام من رمضانَين، على الصحيح للتداخل بالقدر الممكن، وقيل: هذا في رمضان واحد، (فإنْ تَخَلَّلَ التكفير ) بين الوطأين أو الأكلتين ( لا تكفي كفّارةٌ واحدةٌ، في ظاهرِ الرِّواية)؛ لأن التداخل قبل الأداء لا بعده كما في الحدود، كذا في البرهان) وفي (مجمع الروايات» عن « المحيط » : شرب خمراً في
»
رمضان أو زني، فعليه الحد والتعزير والكفارة، لاختلاف الأسباب انتهى.
(۱) تقدم تخريجه ص (٦٥١).
One kaffarah suffices for multiple acts of intercourse and intentional eating on multiple days when no kaffarah intervened between them, even if from two Ramadans, according to the correct view. If kaffarah did intervene, one kaffarah does not suffice according to the apparent narration. Regarding feeding with ability to fast, reflect because when he said to him: 'Are you able to fast two consecutive months?' he said 'No' and one kaffarah suffices for intercourse and intentional eating multiple times on numerous days as long as no kaffarah intervened such as those acts; because kaffarah is legislated for deterrence and it is achieved by one through interference (tadakhul). Even if the days are from two Ramadans, according to the correct view for interference as much as possible. It is said this is for one Ramadan. If kaffarah intervenes between two acts of intercourse or two acts of eating, one kaffarah does not suffice according to the apparent narration, because interference is before performance not after, as in hudud. This is in al-Burhan. And in Majma' al-Riwayat from al-Muhit: If one drinks wine in Ramadan or commits zina, he must undergo hadd, tazeer, and kaffarah due to differing causes. End.
Source pages p. 653

Commentary
This passage discusses the principle of tadakhul (interference) in kaffarah for fasting violations. The ruling states that if a person commits multiple acts of intercourse or intentional eating on different days (e.g., several days in Ramadan) and has not yet performed any kaffarah in between, then one single kaffarah suffices for all those violations. This is the mu'tamad (correct view) according to the Hanafi school. The reasoning is that kaffarah is meant for deterrence (zajr), and one expiation achieves that purpose; multiple expiations would be redundant. This principle applies even if the violations occurred in two different Ramadans (e.g., one violation in Ramadan 1445 and another in Ramadan 1446) as long as no kaffarah was performed in between. However, if a kaffarah was performed after the first violation, then the second violation requires a separate kaffarah. This is based on the principle that tadakhul (merging) applies before the expiation is performed, not after—similar to hudud penalties where multiple offenses merge into one punishment before any punishment is carried out. The passage also references a discussion about the hadith of the Bedouin, where the Prophet accepted one kaffarah for multiple acts? But the main point is the legal ruling. Finally, it notes that if the acts are of different types (e.g., drinking wine and zina), they require separate penalties because the causes differ. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on overlapping kaffarah obligations.

Key Terms
تداخل (tadakhul): The legal principle that multiple obligations of the same type merge into one when the cause is repeated before fulfillment.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani in the six core books.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for violating the fast; here it refers to the obligation of freeing a slave, fasting, or feeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position stated in the passage, if a person has intercourse in Ramadan on two separate days and has not yet performed kaffarah for the first, what is the ruling?
A) Two separate kaffarah are required.
B) One kaffarah suffices for both.
C) No kaffarah is required because the acts are separate.
D) The person must fast two months for each violation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school applies tadakhul to merge multiple kaffarah obligations into one when no expiation has been performed, based on the deterrent purpose of kaffarah.

One Expiation for Multiple Acts in Ramadan: The Principle of Tadakhul
Ruling on multiple acts of intercourse/eating requiring one kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which multiple invalidating acts in Ramadan require only one kaffarah according to the Hanafi school, and explain the evidentiary basis from the hadith.

Core Idea
One expiation covers multiple violations if no expiation separated them — deterrence is achieved once.

In this passage, the author addresses a practical scenario: a person commits multiple acts of intercourse or intentional eating on different days of Ramadan without performing any expiation in between. The Hanafi ruling, based on the principle of tadakhul (overlap), is that a single expiation suffices. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its condition, the exception, and the evidence from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage addresses multiple acts of intercourse or intentional eating on different days in Ramadan. The ruling is that one kaffarah suffices for all acts.
This is the default Hanafi position.
2
Identify the condition for the ruling
The condition for one kaffarah to suffice is that no expiation (kaffarah) has been performed between the acts. If any expiation intervened, each act requires its own kaffarah.
The text says 'لم يَتَخَلَّلْهُ تكفير' – no expiation intervened.
3
Recognize the exception
If expiation did intervene between acts, one kaffarah does not suffice; instead, multiple expiations are required, as per Zahir al-Riwayah.
This is analogous to hudud punishments: overlap before performance but not after.
4
Locate the dalil
The proof is from the hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) asked the man who had intercourse in Ramadan, 'Can you fast two consecutive months?' and did not require multiple expiations for multiple days, indicating that one suffices when no expiation intervenes.
The hadith is cited: 'هَلْ تَسْتَطِيعُ أَنْ تَصُومَ شَهْرَينِ مُتَتَابِعَين؟'
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars restricted this ruling to a single Ramadan; the correct view (sahih) extends it even across two Ramadans, based on the principle of tadakhul as much as possible.
The text says 'على الصحيح' – the correct view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكَفَتْ كفارةً واحدةً، عن جمَاعِ وأكل متعدد في أيامٍ، لم يَتَخَلَّلْهُ تكفير، ولو من رمضانَين، على الصحيح. فإِنْ تَخَلَّلَ التَّكْفِير لا تكفي كفارة واحدة، في ظاهر الرواية.
بالإطعام مع القدرة على الصيام تأمل، لأنه لما قال له: «هَلْ تَسْتَطِيعُ أَنْ تَصُومَ شَهْرَينِ مُتَتَابِعَين؟ قال: لا ) ( وكَفَتْ كفّارةً واحدةً عن جماع وأكل) عمداً (متعدد في أيام) كثيرة و (لم يَتَخَلَّلْهُ) أي: الجماع والأكل عمداً ( تكفير)؛ لأن الكفارة شرعت للزجر وهو يحصل بواحدة للتداخل، (ولــو) كـانت الأيام من رمضانَين، على الصحيح للتداخل بالقدر الممكن، وقيل: هذا في رمضان واحد، (فإنْ تَخَلَّلَ التكفير ) بين الوطأين أو الأكلتين ( لا تكفي كفّارةٌ واحدةٌ، في ظاهرِ الرِّواية)؛ لأن التداخل قبل الأداء لا بعده كما في الحدود، كذا في البرهان) وفي (مجمع الروايات» عن « المحيط » : شرب خمراً في
»
رمضان أو زني، فعليه الحد والتعزير والكفارة، لاختلاف الأسباب انتهى.
And one expiation suffices for multiple acts of intercourse and eating in days, if no expiation intervened, even if from two Ramadans, according to the correct view. If expiation intervened, one expiation does not suffice, in the apparent transmission. With the ability to fast, consider feeding, because when he (the Prophet) said to him: 'Can you fast two consecutive months?' He said: 'No.' And one expiation suffices for multiple acts of intercourse and eating intentionally in many days, and no expiation intervened; because expiation is legislated for deterrence, and that is achieved by one (expiation) due to overlap. Even if the days were from two Ramadans, according to the correct view due to overlapping as much as possible. It was said: This is in one Ramadan. If expiation intervened between two acts of intercourse or two eatings, one expiation does not suffice, in the apparent transmission; because overlap is before performance, not after, as in the case of hudud. Thus in al-Burhan. And in Majma' al-Riwayat from al-Muhit: If one drank wine in Ramadan or committed zina, upon him are hadd, tazir, and kaffarah, due to different causes. End.
Source pages p. 653

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling with proof from the hadith of the man who was unable to fast two consecutive months. The author discusses whether multiple acts of intercourse or eating in Ramadan require a single expiation or multiple expiations. The ruling: If no expiation has been performed between the acts, one expiation suffices, even if the acts occur in different Ramadans. This is because the purpose of expiation is deterrence, and a single expiation achieves that when the acts are continuous without intervening expiation. However, if an expiation was performed between acts, then each act requires its own expiation, similar to the principle in hudud where punishments do not overlap after execution. The proof is from the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered a single expiation for multiple days of intercourse. The mention of wine and zina clarifies that different types of violations (like drinking and zina) each require separate expiations because the causes are different.

Key Terms
الكفارة (al-kaffarah): Expiation for invalidating the fast intentionally; in this text, it refers to the specific penalty of fasting two months or feeding sixty poor.
التداخل (al-tadakhul): Overlap or merging of multiple obligations into one performance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One expiation
B) One expiation for each day
C) Two expiations
D) No expiation

Key Takeaway
One expiation suffices for multiple invalidating acts in Ramadan provided no expiation intervened; this is the principle of tadakhul applied to kaffarah.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
6 min
What Invalidates Fasting and Requires Only Qada' (No Expiation)
Listing and explaining invalidators of fast that require only makeup

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general principle for invalidators that require only qada', list at least five examples, and identify the relied-upon Hanafi view in cases of intra-madhhab disagreement.

Core Idea
Many items break the fast but require only makeup, not expiation—because they lack full nutrition or sexual gratification.

In this lesson, we examine a key taxonomy in Hanafi fiqh of sawm: not every invalidator of the fast demands expiation (kaffarah). The scholars have detailed fifty-seven actions that nullify the fast but obligate only qada' (makeup). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct practice and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle (ḍābiṭ)
Read the opening of the passage where the commentator states the criterion: anything that enters the body without nutritional value or with a deficiency, or that lacks complete sexual gratification, does not require kaffarah.
The principle is the key to distinguishing qada'-only invalidators.
2
Examine the list of examples
Go through the enumerated items: raw rice, dough, flour, salt, clay, pits, cotton, paper, unripe fruit, pebbles, metals, earth, enema, snuff, etc. Note that many are non-nutritive or unripe.
The list is illustrative; the principle applies to similar items.
3
Recognize intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The commentary notes that Imam Muhammad held that eating flour requires kaffarah, while Imam Abu Yusuf held qada' only. The relied-upon view is that of Abu Yusuf, as taken by Abu al-Layth.
Know the muftā bihī position for fatwa.
4
Apply the principle to new items
Using the ḍābiṭ, determine the ruling for modern items like vitamin pills or chewing gum. If they lack nutritional value (e.g., pure cellulose gum), they require only qada'.
Analogize using the illa of deficiency in satisfaction.

باب ما يفسد الصوم ويوجب القضاء من غير كفارة
وهوَ سَبَعَةٌ وخَمسُونَ شَيْئَاً: إذا أكل الصَّائم أرزاً نَيْناً، أو عجيناً، أو دقيقاً، أو ملحاً كثيراً، دفعة، أو طيناً غير أرمني، لم يَعْتَذ أكلَهُ، أَوْ نَوَاةٌ، أَوْ قُطْنَا، أَوْ كَاغِدَاً، أَوْ سَفَرْجَلاً لَمْ يُدرِك ولم يُطْبَحُ، أَوْ جَوْزَةٌ رَطْبَةً أو ابتلع حَصَاةً، أو حديداً، أو تراباً، أو حجراً، أوِ احْتَقَنَ أوِ اسْتَعَطَ، أَوْ أُوحِرَ بصَب شيءٍ فِي حَلْقِهِ، على الأصح.
أداء
باب ما يفسد الصوم ويوجب القضاء من غير كفارة
وضابطه: أن ما ليس فيه غذائية ولا معناها، أو فيه ولكن صحبه عذر شرعي، أو قصور وأوصله إلى جوفه أو دماغه، وما ليس فيه كمال شهوة الفرج لا كفارة به، وقد حصر أفراد ما شمله ذلك بالعد تقريباً، فقال: (وهوَ سَبعةً وخَمسُونَ شَيْئًا) تسهيلاً على المتعلم وهي: (إذا أكل الصَّائم) في رمضان (أرزاً نَيْنَاً أو عجيناً، أو دقيقاً عند أبي يوسف، وبه أخذ الفقيـه أبـو اللـيـث خـلافـاً لمحمد، أو أكل دقيقاً على الصحيح، ودقيق الذرة إذا لته بالسمن والدبس تجـب الـكـفـارة، ودقيـق الحنطة والشعير إذ بل بالماء وخُلط بالسكر تجب به الكفارة، وفي دقيق الجاروش) والأرز قالوا: بأنه تلزمه، كما في « التاتارخانية» . ( أو ) أكل (ملحاً كثيراً، دفعة) على ما قدمناه )، (أو) أكـل طيناً غير أرمني ) و ( لم يَعْتَد أكله، لأنه ليس دواء (أو) أكل (نَوَاةٌ، أو قُطْنَا) أو ابتلع ريقه متغيراً بخضرة، أو صفرة، أو حمرة من عمل الإبريسم (۳) ونحوه، وهو ذاكر لصومه لأنه أكل الصبغ، كذا في والمزيد » ( أو ) أكل ( كاغِدَاً) () ونحوه مما لا يؤكل عادة (أو سَفَرْجَلاً) أو نحوه مـن الثمار التي لا تؤكل قبل النضج (ولم يُطْبَخ ) ولم يملح، (أو جَوْزَةٌ رَطْبَةٌ) ليس لها لبّ، فإن كان لهـا لب فقد علمته، أو ابتلعَ حَصَاةً، أو حديداً) أو نحاساً أو ذهباً أو فضة (أو تراباً، أو حـجـراً)، ولــو زمرداً) ونحوه، وجب القضاء لا الكفارة؛ لقصور الجناية ووجود صورة الفطر، (أوِ احْتَقَنَ، أو استقط) الرواية: بالفتح فيهما الحقنة: صب الدواء في الدبر والسعوط: صب الدواء في الأنف، (أو أو جرَ) وفسره قوله : (بصَبٌ شيءٍ في حَلْقِهِ)، وقوله ( على الأصح) متعلق بالاحتقان ومـا بـعـده، وهـو احتراز عن قول أبي يوسف بوجوب الكفارة، وجه الصحيح أن الكفارة موجب الإفطار صورة ومعنى، والصورة الابتلاع ، كما في ( الكافي»، وهي منعدمة، والنفع المجرد عنها يوجب القضاء فقط.
Chapter on what invalidates fasting and obligates qada' without expiation. And it is fifty-seven things: If the fasting person eats raw rice, or dough, or flour, or a lot of salt at once, or non-Armenian clay that he is not accustomed to eating, or a pit, or cotton, or paper, or unripe quince that has not been cooked, or a fresh walnut, or he swallows a pebble, or iron, or earth, or stone, or he gives himself an enema, or inhales snuff, or is made to pour something into his throat, according to the most correct view. Performance. Chapter on what invalidates fasting and obligates qada' without expiation. And its principle: Whatever has no nutritional value or the like, or has it but accompanied by a legal excuse, or deficiency, and he delivers it to his stomach or brain, and whatever lacks complete sexual desire, there is no expiation for it. He enumerated the individuals covered by that by counting approximately, so he said: 'And it is fifty-seven things' to facilitate the learner. They are: If the fasting person in Ramadan eats raw rice or dough or flour according to Abu Yusuf, and the jurist Abu al-Layth took this, contrary to Muhammad, or he eats flour according to the correct view. Corn flour if mixed with ghee and molasses necessitates expiation. Wheat and barley flour if moistened with water and mixed with sugar necessitates expiation. Regarding flour of coarse grind and rice, they said that it is obligatory, as in al-Tatarkhaniyya. Or he eats a lot of salt at once, as we have presented. Or he eats non-Armenian clay and he is not accustomed to eating it because it is not medicine. Or he eats a pit, or cotton, or swallows his saliva changed by greenness, yellowness, or redness from silk work and the like, while mindful of his fast, because he has eaten the dye. As in al-Mazid. Or he eats paper and the like which is not usually eaten. Or quince or the like of fruits that are not eaten before ripening, and not cooked, and not salted. Or a fresh walnut that has no kernel. If it has a kernel, you have already learned its ruling. Or he swallows a pebble, or iron, or copper, or gold, or silver, or earth, or stone, even if emerald and the like. Qada' is obligatory, not expiation, due to the deficiency of the violation and the existence of the form of breaking the fast. Or he gives himself an enema, or inhales snuff. The pronunciation is with fatha in both. Al-huqna: pouring medicine into the anus. Al-su'ut: pouring medicine into the nose. Or he is made to pour something into his throat. And his statement 'according to the most correct view' is related to the enema and what follows. It is a caveat against the statement of Abu Yusuf who obligated expiation. The basis of the correct view is that expiation is necessitated by breaking the fast in form and meaning. The form is swallowing, as in al-Kafi, and it is absent. The mere benefit apart from form obligates only qada'.
Source pages p. 654

Commentary
This passage is a definition and listing of what invalidates the fast and requires only qada' without expiation. The commentator begins by stating the general principle: anything that enters the body without nutritional value or with a deficiency, or that lacks the completeness of sexual gratification, does not require expiation but only qada'. Then he lists examples, noting that there are fifty-seven such items. The list includes eating raw rice, dough, flour, a lot of salt, clay that is not normally eaten, pits, cotton, paper, unripe fruit, swallowing pebbles, iron, earth, stones, etc. The commentator also mentions differences among Hanafi scholars: for example, regarding flour, Abu Yusuf holds that it requires only qada', while Muhammad holds that it requires expiation. The relied-upon view is that of Abu Yusuf. He also discusses enema and snuff, where the correct view is that they require only qada', contrary to Abu Yusuf's earlier view that they require expiation. The reasoning is that expiation is only for full breaking of the fast in both form and meaning; these acts lack the form of ingestion (swallowing) or the meaning of nutrition.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qada'): Making up the missed fast after Ramadan, without expiation penalty.
الإفساد (al-ifṣād): Invalidating the fast by any of the listed actions.
الكفارة (al-kaffārah): Expiation for intentionally breaking a Ramadan fast by eating, drinking, or sexual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi view, if a fasting person eats raw rice intentionally, what is required?
A) Qada' only
B) Qada' and kaffarah
C) No penalty
D) Kaffarah only

Key Takeaway
The invalidators of fasting that require only qada' are those that lack full nutritional value or complete sexual gratification; expiation is reserved for full satisfaction of appetite or sexual desire.
